Pet therapy dogs: a calming canine caravan comes to Concordia
http://www.concordia.ca/cunews/main/stories/exams/calm-inducing-canine-caravan-pet-therapy.html?rootnav=news
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i1_Nov_2017_12:00:00_EDT
Finals can be stressful. And while there are lots of ways to beat exam stress, from exercise to meditation, is there anything more comforting than a furry friend with a wagging tail?
In November and December, the Webster Library and Georges P. Vanier Library will welcome several pet-therapy dogs from the Blue Ribbon Canine Centre to help students relax.
Webster Library (outside LB-237)
Wednesday, November 22 – 11:30 a.m. to 1:30 p.m.
Tuesday, November 28 – 11:30 a.m. to 1:30 p.m.
Vanier Library (outside VL-101)
Thursday, November 30, – 12 to 2 p.m.
Wednesday, December 6 – 12 to 2 p.m.

2017-11-13 14:00:00
Undergrads: Test a new Library tutorial and get a $10 Starbucks gift card for 1 hour of your time
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i30_Oct_2017_13:00:00_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i30_Oct_2017_13:00:00_EDT
We've created a new online tutorial for undergraduate students to help you with your research projects. It covers:
How to choose a research topic, come up with a research topic and find the right places to search
Search techniques
Finding articles
Finding books
Finding other types of sources and specialized information
Strategies for reading, writing and note-taking
Citing
We want to make sure that the tutorial meets the needs of undergraduate students, so we’d like your feedback. Sign up so we can set up a time for you to come to the library and test a couple of sections from the tutorial. It should take about 1 hour of your time and you will receive a $10 gift card from Starbucks.

6 Oct 2017 15:00:00 EDT
Call for proposals for public art
https://library.concordia.ca/about/visualization-call-for-proposals/
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i17_Oct_2017_15:00:00_EDT
The Concordia Library is seeking to commission a content creator or team to create an engaging custom public audio-visual art piece to celebrate the launch of the Visualization Studio and the completion of the Webster Library renovation. The visualization will be displayed on the touch-interactive wall of the Visualization Studio, on the third floor of the Webster Library, and will be visible to all visitors. It will be one of the main visualizations showcasing the new space.
The Concordia Library welcomes artists, creatives, scientists, engineers, interdisciplinary scholars to apply and encourages bold, creative and playful projects.
Applications will be open until November 14, 2017, and can be submitted by email.
Selected works must be operational by the end of February.

14 Sep 2017 17:19:22 EDT
New online subscription: The Chronicle of Higher Education
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i14_Sep_2017_17:19:22_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i14_Sep_2017_17:19:22_EDT
Concordia University Library has subscribed to :
Daily reports on developments in higher education, information technology, and distance education in America including faculty/administrative postings.
The full text of the current issue of The Chronicle is available every Monday morning, following the Friday print publication. The site features an archive of premium articles of the last 28 years of The Chronicle.
The license allows unlimited simultaneous users.
One note about creating an account using your e-mail domain access – if any users have already created an account at Chronicle.com with their @concordia.ca e-mail address,
that account will automatically link to the site license so they will not need to create a new one.
If they have their credentials saved in their browser, they might just need to log out
and log back into the site to refresh their cookies.
If they don’t remember their password, they can reset it through the “Forgot your password?” link on the log-in page.

The Webster Library's media, curriculum and microform collections as well as maps and atlases and DLI and Kardex file catalogues are currently unavailable. There may be delays of up to a week obtaining these materials via requests for holds. We apologize for any inconvenience this may cause.

Sticker party

http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Sep_2017_12:20:56_EDT

This intro will walk you through the basics of using vector graphics. You'll then print your design as a small vinyl decal (cut-out sticker). 10 Oct 2017 12:20:56 EDT
2017-11-17 15:00:00
Intro to Sketchup
https://www.eventbrite.ca/e/intro-to-sketchup-registration-38670028095
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i10_Oct_2017_12:20:56_EDT
Speaker: Ruolin Wang, Technology Sandbox Assistant
Sketchup is a popular 3D modeling software which has a wide range of uses in architectural design, interior design, civil and mechanical engineering. Compared to other 3D modeling software, Sketchup is easily to learn and supported by a friendly interface. Compelling walkthroughs, house staining and detailed models can be created in this software; Sketchup files can also be exported to other simulation software, such as Energy Plus, Wufi, Transys and others.
This workshop will get you started on the right foot with Sketchup! We will look at basic commands to model the interior and exterior of buildings, and model a quick example. Finally we will look at some useful Sketchup plugins, for example one plugin makes it simple to 3D print your creation.
Please bring a laptop with Sketchup installed on it. You can install Sketchup beforehand (30-day trial) using this link:
Open to everyone. 120 minutes.
Friday, November 17, 1 - 3 p.m.
Webster Library, LB-205
(Starts Oct. 27).

Intro to Linux
https://www.eventbrite.ca/e/intro-to-linux-registration-38048841108
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Sep_2017_12:20:55_EDT
Speaker: Sean Cooney, Technology Sandbox Technician, Concordia University Library
Have you heard of Linux and want to know more, or you haven’t heard of Linux but the words “free operating system” spark your interest? Maybe you already know a little bit about Linux and want to learn the basics of how to use it; everyone is welcome at our Intro to Linux workshop! In this workshop we’ll cover a bit of background of who, what, when, and why, and then go into some details on the ways in which using the operating system differs from Mac and Windows. Raspberry Pi computers for using and experimenting with Linux will be provided.
Open to everyone. 120 minutes.
Tuesday, November 14, 2 - 4 p.m.
Webster Library, LB-205
(Starts Oct. 24).

3D modelling 102: OpenSCAD
https://www.eventbrite.ca/e/3d-modelling-102-openscad-registration-38048756856
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Sep_2017_12:20:54_EDT
Speaker: Sean Cooney, Technology Sandbox Technician, Concordia University Library
So you want to model things in 3D (be it for 3D printing, digital art, blueprints, or for video-game content), but you’re unfamiliar with how to do it or the software you’re using doesn’t give you the fine control you need?
Come to our workshop. OpenSCAD is free, open-source software for detailed, programmatically defined, primitive based rendering software.
If that sounds complicated, you will be pleasantly surprised at how easy and intuitive the software is once you get started. Please bring a laptop you can install software on.
Open to everyone. 120 minutes.
Thursday, November 9, 2 - 4 p.m.
Webster Library, LB-205
(Starts Oct. 19).

2017-11-17 15:30:00
Hyperbolic space crochet
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i2_Nov_2017_12:20:53_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i2_Nov_2017_12:20:53_EDT
This is nerdy-math-crafting like you have never seen it before!
Drop by the Technology Sandbox in November to learn how to crochet a model of hyperbolic space. This is nerdy-math-crafting like you have never seen it before! Warning: other mathematical models may also be explored, and you may leave with a greater appreciation for the connection between textiles and computing. We will teach you a little bit about hyperbolic space and the basic crochet stitches to get started. Drop by from 2 - 3:30 p.m. on November 8-10, 13-14, or 16-17 to get expert assistance with your project. Basic supplies provided and no prior crochet or math skills required!

Speaker: Tina Salameh, Technology Analyst, Concordia University Library
In this 3-hour-long workshop, we will teach you everything you need to know about soldering to take your upcoming electronics project from the breadboard to the real world.
We will learn about the tools of the trade and the techniques that will make your soldering solid and reliable.
By the end of our workshop you will have built one or two fun projects you can take home, and we will show you where you can go from there!

Safe Sexting: Digital intimacy on your own terms
https://www.eventbrite.ca/e/safe-sexting-digital-intimacy-on-your-own-terms-registration-38601108956
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i6_Oct_2017_12:30:54_EDT
As our sex lives increasingly play out in the digital world, how do we adapt safe practices to screens and code? This sex-positive workshop will give you practical tips for preserving your privacy online by breaking down the pros and cons of various applications used for sharing pictures and chatting, and videocalling. The idea is to empower us with a clearer understanding of the potential risks and ways to mitigate them, in continuity with sex ed for in the analogue world.
As a bonus, the takeaways from this digital hygiene crash course extend beyond your intimate life.
This workshop is presented by the Tiger Lotus Coop . Speakers will be Maroussia Lévesque and Tina Salameh.
Maroussia Lévesque is a lawyer and researcher at the crossroads of law and technology, with a background in interactive arts. She lead teams of designers, artists and programmers for the Obx lab for experimental media at the Hexagram research-creation institute. She was called to the Quebec Bar in 2013 and clerked at the Quebec Court of Appeal for the Chief Justice. She was the intelligence analyst at the Quebec inquiry commission on the protection of journalists’ sources, examining law enforcement’s electronic surveillance practices. She currently focuses on algorithmic fairness and is a member of IEEE’s working group on algorithmic accountability.
Tina Salameh is a Computational Arts double major Concordia alumna. She has spent the past 8 years working in startups, walking the lines between Art, Design and Technology. In her free time, she fights for freedom of speech and digital rights in the Middle East and runs workshops on digital privacy.
She loves things that are open source and things that are playful (and cats with laser eyes). She’s currently helping the Library build the Visualization Studio -- a space for interactivity, immersion, data visualization, research and many other endeavours.
While this is a free is event there is a $5 suggested donation.
Open to everyone. 120 minutes.
Thursday, October 19, 6 - 8 pm
Webster Library, LB-211
.

Using RefWorks for Graduates - Citations and Bibliographies Simplified
https://www.concordia.ca/students/gradproskills/workshops/details.html?subject_area=GPLL&catalog_number=236
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i27_Jul_2017_15:30:53_EDT
Workshop for graduate students.
In this hands-on workshop you will learn how to use RefWorks, a web-based tool that you can use to organize the references you find in library catalogues and databases, insert citations in your papers, and prepare bibliographies or reference lists quickly and effectively, in a wide variety of citation styles (e.g. APA, MLA, Chicago, et cetera). We will also discuss how to integrate RefWorks with Microsoft Word using RefWorks' Write'n-Cite tool, and how to share your RefWorks folders and citations (e.g., for collaborative projects or to disseminate reading lists). No experience with RefWorks is necessary.
Thursday, October 19, 1:30 - 3:30pm
Webster Library, LB-207
.

2017-09-26
Using RefWorks for Graduates - Citations and Bibliographies Simplified
https://www.concordia.ca/students/gradproskills/workshops/details.html?subject_area=GPLL&catalog_number=236
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i27_Jul_2017_12:30:50_EDT
Workshop for graduate students.
In this hands-on workshop you will learn how to use RefWorks, a web-based tool that you can use to organize the references you find in library catalogues and databases,
insert citations in your papers, and prepare bibliographies or reference lists quickly and effectively, in a wide variety of citation styles (e.g. APA, MLA, Chicago, et cetera).
We will also discuss how to integrate RefWorks with Microsoft Word using RefWorks' Write'n-Cite tool,
and how to share your RefWorks folders and citations (e.g., for collaborative projects or to disseminate reading lists). No experience with RefWorks is necessary.
Tuesday, September 26, 9:30 - 11:30am
Webster Library, LB-207
.

2017-09-25
Canadian Statistics and Microdata for the Social Sciences
https://www.concordia.ca/students/gradproskills/workshops/details.html?subject_area=GPLL&catalog_number=235
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i27_Jul_2017_12:20:50_EDT
Workshop for graduate students.
This workshop will focus on the main sources of social statistics in Canada, namely Statistics Canada's Website, the Canadian Census, the National Household Survey (NHS), and CANSIM.
Provincial statistics (Institut de la Statistique du Québec) will also be mentioned.
The second part of the presentation will present the concept of microdata and introduce students to data available through the Data Liberation Initiative (DLI).
We will review the best methods to identify relevant surveys. The various types of data files (PUMFs, Master Files) will be described and students will be shown how to access those files via the Odesi database,
or by going to the Research Data Centre at McGill (QICSS). There will be a demonstration of Odesi which will focus on searching the platform for surveys and individual variables and on downloading datasets and
associated documentation.
Monday, September 25, 10 - 11:30am
Webster Library, LB-207
.

Museum technology: 3D scans and prints, virtual reality, GIFs and stolen art
https://www.eventbrite.ca/e/museum-technology-3d-scans-and-prints-virtual-reality-gifs-and-stolen-art-tickets-37423104513
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i29_Aug_2017_12:20:44_EDT
Speaker: Zia Davidian (Master of Information Studies candidate, McGill University)
This workshop will introduce you to the technology available in the Sandbox, through examples influenced by art, museology, and cultural heritage. We’ll explore GIFs, stolen art, and ancient ruins in VR;
we’ll create 3D scans of ourselves; and we’ll 3D print miniature versions of priceless antiquities. Come explore the exciting intersection of technology and the arts! This workshop is designed as an introduction to the space;
not everyone will leave with a print. Open to everyone. 120 minutes.

Raspberry Pi data logging
https://www.eventbrite.ca/e/raspberry-pi-data-logging-tickets-37429625016
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i29_Aug_2017_12:20:43_EDT
Speaker: Jasia Stuart, Technology Analyst, Concordia University Library
Get started with the Raspberry Pi in this quick, practical overview focusing on using sensors and logging data. We will use a light sensor and atmospheric pressure sensor to gather some data with a short Python script.
You will walk away from this class with a better understanding of what Raspberry Pi computers are and how you can harness their power for data collection.
This is an introductory workshop and no prior programming or electronics skills are required, Raspberry Pi computers are provided for the workshop.
This workshop is also open to McGill students as it is presented as part of Science Literacy Week.
Open to everyone. 120 minutes.

Location

Tuesday, September 19
2 - 4 p.m.
Webster Library, LB-211

New database: East India Company: Trade Governance and Empire, 1600-1947
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i14_Jul_2017_13:41:38_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i14_Jul_2017_13:41:38_EDT
(Image: , with the Roads, by Thomas Jefferys)
Concordia University Library has acquired the Adam Matthew Digital database East India Company Module 1: Trade Governance and Empire, 1600-1947:
A collection of India Office Records from the British Library, 1600 to 1947.
Beginning with the Company's establishment by a charter from Queen Elizabeth I;
traces its first voyages east, early attempts to trade in the Spice Islands (Indonesia), India and Japan, and skirmishes with pirates and rival trading companies.
The licence allows unlimited simultaneous users.
.

Course Reserves Room at the Vanier Library
Books from the 4th floor of the Webster Library (LB-4) that were housed in offsite storage to facilitate the Webster Library Transformation will return to the Webster Library on September 5.
Keep in mind that from August 8 to September 4, Concordia Library staff will not be able to treat your hold requests or your course reserves requests, as the items will be inaccessible.

2017-07-04
Some Library services will be closed during midday on Tuesday, July 4
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i3_Jul_2017_17:41:38_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i3_Jul_2017_17:41:38_EDT
At Webster Library, the Loans & Returns and Interlibrary Loans services will be closed from 11:45 a.m. to 2:30 p.m.
At Vanier Library, the Circulation and Special Collections services will be closed from 11:30 a.m. to 3:00 p.m.
To borrow books, please use the self-checkout station.
Any items due for return during this period should be returned when the service reopens. Fines will be adjusted accordingly.
For additional information, consult with staff at the Ask Us desk.
This brief closure is to permit members of the Concordia University Library Employees Union to attend a General Assembly on a tentative new collective agreement.

the Concordia Library Researcher-in-Residence program was created to promote research in the library and the use of research by practitioners. The program offers the opportunity for scholars, information professionals,
or doctoral students to focus on an area of inquiry in a supportive and enriching environment, and to interact with Concordia Library staff and its resources.

https://www.eventbrite.ca/e/intro-to-openscad-tickets-35021135158
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i1_Jun_2017_12:20:48_EDT
So you want to model things in 3D (be it for 3D printing, digital art, blueprints, or for video-game content) but you're unfamiliar with how to do it or the software you're using doesn't
give you the fine control you need. Come to our workshop. OpenSCAD is free, open-source software for detailed, programmatically defined, primitive based rendering software.
If that sounds complicated, you will be pleasantly surprised at how easy and intuitive the software is once you get started. Please bring a laptop you can install software on.

This crash course will teach you to navigate the magical world of Photoshop and get you up and running as fast as possible.
We'll learn to navigate the interface, select objects, manipulate images, do color corrections, draw with vectors, make gifs and anything else you're curious about. Come join us if you've always wanted to learn to

This workshop is BYOL (Bring Your Own Laptop). Please install Photoshop on your laptop beforehand. You can download the trial version here:
We're going to be running Photoshop CC for this workshop, but you should be able to follow along with older versions.
Please note that loan laptops from the library will not work for this workshop as they do not have Photoshop installed on them.

sending you selfies you will start to get a feeling for how to put this tiny, inexpensive computer to work in both practical and fanciful ways.
This is a good workshop for starting with a Raspberry Pi. No pet ownership actually required. Laptop recommended.

2017-04-23
Webster Library Exhibition: Booked 5
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i31_Mar_2017_12:10:34_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i31_Mar_2017_12:10:34_EDT
Webster Library – 2nd floor
Booked 5
The book works in this year's installation of BOOKED include a diverse range of one-of-a-kind objects produced by students in the course DART 280 – Investigations in Typographic Design
taught by Pata Macedo.
Centered on the theme of Winter in the world we live in, the book format provides a space for students to bring together narratives and imagery with various techniques including printmaking, graphic design and typography, bookbinding, photography, textiles or sculpture. These disparate constructions underline the boundless possibilities inherent in the book format, offering a multilayered reading experience for the viewer.
Curated by Pata Macedo and Melinda Reinhart

2017-04-28
Library Research Forum
http://library.concordia.ca/about/staff/forum/index.php
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i23_Mar_2017_12:20:43_EDT
Since 2002, Concordia's Library Research Forum has provided librarians, archivists, graduate students, teaching faculty, and information professionals with an opportunity to describe and promote their completed or in-progress research, practical case studies or projects. The Forum also provides a venue for researchers to seek suggestions for enhancing their research interests, to identify potential new partners for projects, to test the effectiveness of their undertakings, and to promote research in academic libraries.
Friday, April 28,	9 a.m. - 4:45 p.m.
Loyola Jesuit Hall and Conference Centre, Loyola Campus
.

Portable standing desks now available to borrow at the Library
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i14_Mar_2017_10:20:43_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i14_Mar_2017_10:20:43_EDT
Lightweight cardboard portable standing desks are available for loan at Concordia University Library. Easy to fold and carry, these desks allow you to work while standing up.
The desks were purchased with the support of the , which is funded by undergraduate students.
For more information about these desks, including a video on how to set them up, see the following link:
.
There are 3 desks available for loan at Vanier Library and 5 at Webster Library. Loans will be for a maximum of 8 hours, but same day only (no overnight loans).
Loans after 1 p.m. will automatically be due a half hour before the circulation desks close.
We encourage you to try the desks out and give us !

2017-02-26
Grand reopening of LB-2 West
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i15_Feb_2017_14:20:43_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i15_Feb_2017_14:20:43_EDT
The third of four phases of the Webster Library
Transformation will be complete once LB-2 West reopens to the public on
Wednesday, February 22 at 9 a.m. Earlier this year, LB-2 East and the Library’s
main staircase reopened.
Temporary closure of Webster LibraryIn order to move the Library’s Circulation
Desk, Reference and Information Desk, and the Interlibrary Loans department to
LB-2, the Webster Library will close on Sunday, February 19 at 11 p.m. and
reopen on Wednesday, February 22 at 9 a.m.  We chose to do this during
Reading Week to lessen the impact on students. The
and
the
will have regular opening hours during
that time.
Restoration of permanent main entranceWith this reopening, entrance to the Webster
Library will return to its permanent state. Students will enter the library
from the main staircase and be able to take internal Library stairs or
elevators to higher floors. This will reduce the crowding of the elevator on
LB-1 and the fire escape stairways will no longer be needed.
New service pointsWhen visitors enter the Library from the main
staircase, they will be greeted immediately by the new service area for
This is a re-visioning of our former Information and Reference Desk
and will be the new place to go for help in the Library. In fact, three
services will be offered at the Ask Us desk:
General
and directional information and basic reference
Reference
questions and research assistance
Technical
questions relating to equipment and software.
Also coming to LB-2 is the new Loans & Returns
desk, a permanent installation of the former Circulation Desk. Book displays
and self-checkout machines will be nearby.
The Interlibrary Loans department will have a
new permanent home on LB-2 as well.
Technology focusA brand new service will be launched on February
22: the . It's a place for the Concordia community to try out emerging
technologies and cutting-edge equipment. Learn about 3D printing, electronics,
or digital music by attending a workshop. Work on your personal tech project,
explore virtual reality with headsets we provide, or tell our digital die
cutter to print your vinyl decal. It's a community technology space where
everyone can learn by doing, by making, by playing, and by sharing knowledge
with each other. .
Exciting new technologies will be added to the
Library on LB-2: the , digital signage and
wayfinding kiosks, and an immersive .
In the next few weeks, an additional group
study room and classroom will be opening on LB-2 West.
Art is another focus on LB-2, with a new space
for exhibitions in the Library as well as a renewal of the
from 1992.
What’s next? Phase 4/4 is underway since
December 2016. LB-4 is currently closed in order to complete renovations. LB-3
West will be closing shortly for renovations. The Webster Library Transformation will be complete at the end of 2017.

Lots of things, but once you experience the magic of your cat (or dog, or goldfish!) sending you selfies you will start to get a feeling for how to put this tiny, inexpensive computer to work in both practical and fanciful ways. Introduction to wearables: Arduino 101
http://library.concordia.ca/help/workshops/technology-sandbox.php?guid=arduino
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i15_Feb_2017_12:20:32_EDT
​Come and transform an item of clothing into a blinking, colour-changing, wearable device. If you want to take your creation home with you,
you will need purchase materials similar to
as well as the fabric item in which you would like to embed the electronics.
If you are not ready to take that leap, follow along on one of our Arduino Uno kits. Please bring your laptop or sign one out before the workshop.
No prior programming, electronics or sewing experience required! For people just wanting a simple introduction to Arduino, this is a great place to start.
Tuesday, March 14,	10 a.m. - 12 p.m.
Webster Library, LB-211.00

LB-2 East now open to the public
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i18_Jan_2017_12:18:18_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i18_Jan_2017_12:18:18_EDT
Webster LB-2 East (Bishop side) is now open to the public.
Access to LB-2 from LB-3 is through the North (De Maisonneuve side) internal library staircase only. For those requiring elevator access, they will need to contact Security.
On LB-2 are housed the following collections:
Reference
Standards
Journals
Government documents
Microforms (microform reading equipment will not be available)
Curriculum and Media collections (including kits, music CDs and scores)
The main staircase from LB-1 to LB-2 is now open, but since LB-2 West is still under construction, the main staircase leads visitors to the emergency staircase to the main entrance of the Library on LB-3.
Users and staff will continue to use the emergency staircase between LB-2 and LB-3 to reach the main entrance of the Library.
Elevator #1 from LB-0/LB-1 to LB-3 will remain as well.

2017-01-17
LB-2 East reopening on Tuesday, January 17 at noon
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i11_Jan_2017_15:18:18_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i11_Jan_2017_15:18:18_EDT
Webster LB-2 East (Bishop side) is scheduled to open on Tuesday, January 17 at 12:00 p.m. to the public.
Access to LB-2 from LB-3 will be through the North (De Maisonneuve side) internal library staircase only. For those requiring elevator access, they will need to contact Security.
On LB-2 are housed the following collections:
Reference
Standards
Journals
Government documents
Microforms (microform reading equipment will not be available)
Curriculum and Media collections (including kits, music CDs and scores)
Holds can be placed on Curriculum and Media collections material for retrieval by using the
in the
or the .
Should you need access to any of the other collections before Tuesday at 12:00 p.m.
(e.g., reference, journals, microforms etc., any material which is on LB-2 with the status “Lib Use Only” in the catalogue), please do the following:
Monday - Friday: make a request via
using the form for
“the full volume of a periodical”;
in the field for volume/date enter “LB-2”. You will get an email when the material is retrieved and it will be held at the Circulation Desk for you to pick up.
Saturday - Sunday: consult with staff at the Webster Circulation Desk. It will depend on the time of day and the number of staff as to whether material can be retrieved.
For access to microform readers before Tuesday at 12 pm, you may want to go to the Vanier Library.
You could make a request to have microforms in the Webster collection moved to Vanier via the Article Delivery service (using the option for “the full volume of a periodical”).
Otherwise it may be simpler to wait until January 17 for access.
The main staircase from LB-1 to LB-2 will also reopen on Wednesday, January 18 at 12:00 p.m.
Users and staff will continue to use the emergency staircase between LB-2 and LB-3 to reach the main entrance of the Library. Elevator #1 from LB-0/LB-1 to LB-3 will remain as well.

Webster Library Exhibition: Lori Beavis - Cultural Collateral: identity, community and belonging
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i6_Dec_2016_12:32:14_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i6_Dec_2016_12:32:14_EDT
Lori Beavis
Cultural Collateral: identity, community and belonging
December 5 – January 10, 2016
This installation represents my grandmother's experience of living at and having to leave Hiawatha, the Mississauga First Nation in central Ontario where she was born and raised. Principally I am attempting to illustrate her experience of having her identity as an Indigenous woman taken from her when in 1930 she married my grandfather a non-Native man of Welsh origin.
Very briefly, this meant that she was disenfranchised from her Indigenous heritage and her community. This was the same experience for many, many women across the country who were also subject to the patriarchal and assimilationist rules of this government act.
This installation marks the deeply troubling experience of my grandmother, her husband and children being formally requested to leave the Hiawatha Reserve. In the mid-1930s my grandmother and her young family had been allowed to return to the Reserve to care for my great-grandfather (Henry Cowie) during his ill-health. They lived there for almost five years despite the official policy of having no status and no rights – the family became part of the community with my mother and her siblings attending the on-reserve school. However, at the time of my great-grandfather's death in 1941 Laura and her family were compelled to leave the Reserve and relinquish any rights and property there within a very short time frame. This installation documents through family archival materials and found objects the things that she was able to take with her when she officially left the Reserve.
However, like most family stories there are extenuating circumstances – Laura never relinquished her identity as a Mississauga woman and she rejoiced when she regained her Status late in life. In addition, she never stayed away for very long as throughout her life she visited and kept up the friendships that had been established in her childhood.
The objects shown here are a representation of what she was able to take with her, there are also domestic objects that reflect the stories and memories that I have of her. Through these various objects, I am (I hope), demonstrating my grandmother's on-going sense of herself as a proud Mississauga woman and the fact that one's identity cannot be taken away.
- Lori Beavis-

2016-12-08
27th Annual Concordia University Library Christmas Auction
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i23_Nov_2016_15:38:18_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i23_Nov_2016_15:38:18_EDT
Concordia University Library Christmas Auction Committee is holding its annual Christmas Auction!
Every year the Library Staff of Concordia University Library hold an auction to raise funds for charitable organizations in our community.
This is the 27th year that we are holding our fund raising Auction to benefit:
Auberge Madeleine, Can Serve Foundation, Chez Doris, CODE (Canadian Organization for Development through Education),
Concordia University Centre for the Arts in Human Development (CAHD), Multi-Faith Chaplaincy and Financial Aids and Awards, Dans la Rue,
the Gazette Christmas Fund, Operation Eyesight Universal, OXFAM, Sun Youth, and the Women's Centre of Montreal.
Auctionable items have included signed hockey sticks from the Montreal Canadiens to books, CDs, jams, original paintings, hand crafted jewelry, cosmetics,
and gift certificates to downtown restaurants. Many one-of-a-kind items have been auctioned off! There is something for everyone!
Admission: $2
Food will be available for purchase as well.
Library staff at the 2015 Christmas Auction

Seeking nominations for staff award
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i22_Nov_2016_15:38:18_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i22_Nov_2016_15:38:18_EDT
Here is an opportunity to recognize the good service you have received from the Library.
Nominations are now being sought for the .
This award was established to encourage and reward staff currently working for Concordia Library whose commitment and professionalism reflect the values exemplified
by Freda Otchere.
This award is made possible through the generous gift of Dr. Dan Otchere, Associate Professor of Economics at Concordia University,
who created the Freda Otchere Endowment Fund in 2010 in honour of his wife. From 1970 to 2004,
Freda Otchere served the Concordia University Library as cataloguer and Head of Database Maintenance.
Her exemplary service to the Concordia community is warmly remembered, and provides the model by which nominees are identified.
Anyone may nominate a library employee for this award.
See also:
Library staff September 2015

Date and time: December 8, 12-2pm
Admission: $2
Food will be available for purchase as well.

iZoom Low Vision Screen Magnifier
JAWS (Job Access with Speech) Screen Reader
ClaroRead Plus for text-to-speech and writing help

Webster Library: satellite site for Sightings (Ellen Gallery) exhibition
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i29_Sep_2016_10:00:14_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i29_Sep_2016_10:00:14_EDT
SIGHTINGS 18 THIS IS A ▢ TO BE COMPLETED AT HOME
September 12 – November 6, 2016
A project by Maude Johnson and Didier Morelli
A satellite site of the exhibition, located on the 5th floor of the Webster Library (passage area, south side), displays a consultation copy of the book Teaching and Learning as Performing Arts (1970) and presents the video Teaching and Learning as Performing Arts Part II: Travelin' Light – It's a Dance, Really (1979), courtesy of the Western Front (Vancouver). The two collaborators used a
to inform and share their research in real time.
More information on the .

31 Aug 2016 12:39:18 EDT
New tablets located next to group study rooms on LB3 and LB5 allow you to check in, reserve, modify or end your booking
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i31_Aug_2016_12:39:18_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i31_Aug_2016_12:39:18_EDT
As part of the
project, touch screens for group study room reservations are now beside group study rooms on LB3 and LB5. Don't forget to check in with your netname and password when you arrive. Check-ins help us avoid having booked but empty rooms which prevent others from making reservations. If a check-in is not made within the first 30 minutes of a reservation, the reservation will be cancelled in order to liberate the space for others.
.

Archives of Montreal jazz legend Russ Dufort added to Special Collections
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i3_Aug_2016_12:39:18_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i3_Aug_2016_12:39:18_EDT
Photo credit: Russ Dufort playing drums with the Johnny Holmes Band at Victoria Hall, 1946 (P016-02-74)
Special Collections is pleased to announce that the
is now available for consultation. This fonds is the latest addition to the Libraries' jazz collections.
Russell (Russ) Dufort was a drummer in a number of significant Montreal jazz bands, including the Johnny Holmes Orchestra and the Stardusters. He also played with renowned pianist and composer Oscar Peterson. The scores, photographs, correspondence, and other items in this fonds complement those materials found in the .
To make an appointment to consult the materials in the Russell (Russ) Dufort fonds, please contact .

20 May 2016 13:20:00 EDT
Webster Library Exhibition: Where are Books Going …
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i20_May_2016_13:20:00_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i20_May_2016_13:20:00_EDT
Where are Books Going …
May 14 – June 30, 2016
Library entrance, 3rd floor
Book works created by Katie Lefevre, MA student in Art Education
Working with recycled copies of duplicate books, the artist questions how books are defined in a world of increasing technology. She explores the potential of book arts as mixed media sculptures that engage with the physical form of texts, as well as the psychological and spiritual content of their narratives.

10 May 2016 14:39:18 EDT
New temporary entrances for the Webster Library
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i10_May_2016_14:39:18_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i10_May_2016_14:39:18_EDT
As part of Phase 3 of the
project, LB-2 is closed for renovations. The main staircase entrance to the Webster Library is closed until February 2017 as it is part of this phase of construction.
Visitors may enter the library via the temporary entrance on MacKay St. which provides stairs from street level to LB-3 or via the LB-1 elevator closest to the bookstore which goes directly to LB-3.
Signage has been posted on MacKay St. and on LB-1 indicating the temporary entrances.
Services that used to be on LB-2 (Circulation Desk, Reference Desk and the Course Reserves Room), as well as the book drop and newspapers display, are now on LB-3 in the MacKay St. / de Maisonneuve St. W. corner.
Phase 3 of the renovations is probably the largest of the 4 phases since it will encompass all of LB-2, including the entrance, the circulation and reference desks, and the main staircase. Work started on LB-2 Bishop St. side in March and on MacKay St. on May 10. The targeted date of completion is January 31, 2017.

be unavailable
for approximately 4 hours during the early morning of Thursday, May 19,
between the hours of 7:00 and 11:00 a.m.

26 Apr 2016 16:32:40 EDT
2016-05-09
Due to renovations, Webster Library will be closed from Saturday, May 7 at 9:00 p.m. until Tuesday, May 10 at 9:00 a.m.
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i26_Apr_2016_16:32:40_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i26_Apr_2016_16:32:40_EST
Users who need to return items that are due during the closed period can do so at one of the two book drops located on LB2;
items returned during the closed period will not incur fines. Short term loan items (such as laptops, reserves) borrowed just
before the closing period will be due after the library re-opens on the morning of May 10.
On May 7, the Reserve Room gates will close at 5pm but the Library will remain open for study until 9pm.
As part of the Webster Transformation, the art at the top of the LB2 stairs was dismantled for restoration.
The reinstallation of the mural is scheduled for the end of Phase 4.
Library book drops can be used at all times. Not to be used to return laptops.
Starting Tuesday, May 10 at 9am, the main staircase will be closed for renovations. Users will access the Webster Library via the emergency staircase located to the left of the
Mackay door.
Starting Tuesday, May 10 at 9am, the Circulation and Reference/Information Desks and the Reserve Room will be located to LB3 (corner de Maisonneuve and Mackay).
In order to facilitate the return of books, additional drop-in boxes will be available on LB1 on May 10. Items (books, course packs, and laptops) checked out and for
which the return date is May 8 or 9 will have their due dates changed to May 10.
If not returned before 4:45pm, laptops checkout on Saturday, May 7 will have a return date of Tuesday, May 10, 11am.

Winning poems from the Webster Library Transformation Poetry Contest
http://library.concordia.ca/poetry/
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i21_Apr_2016_10:32:28_EDT
We are delighted by the enthusiastic reception that the Poetry Contest received.  One hundred and twenty-three poems were submitted by 81 poets and as you can well imagine, the jury members had quite a challenging task at hand.
But more important than statistics is the fact that many poems were beautifully crafted.  After much deliberation and discussion, our jury members selected the three winning submissions and another four that received an Honourable Mention.  .  The winning submissions will be posted on the wrap-around of the Library staircase, in the Vanier Library, in the Grey Nuns Reading Room and several other locations.

Webster Library Exhibition: Scripting
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Apr_2016_10:32:28_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Apr_2016_10:32:28_EDT
Collaboration: Ceramics 398 and Art History 264
April 14 – May 7, 2016
Scripting brings together both ceramic and art history students and
their visual and written works in a collaborative environment.
It was conceived as a two-part exercise, involving the initial making
of the ceramic works by the ceramic students, followed by an art
historical/critical response to them written by ceramic history students.
Dr. Susan Surette, ARTH 264: Ceramic Tiles (Ad)dressing Surfaces –
Aspects of Ceramic History
Professor Linda Swanson, CERA 398: 2D3D - Special Topics in Ceramics

2016-05-10
Grad Pro Skills: Library Skills & Resources: Maximize Your Graduate Research Potential
http://gradstudies.concordia.ca/gradproskills/workshops/workshop/GPRM231
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Apr_2016_12:16:22_EDT
This workshop aims to ensure that participants do not
miss out on the little-known research tools and tricks which can be indispensable
for effective graduate level research at Concordia in all subject areas. We will cover
essentials such as:
Pinpointing the best spots on the library web site for graduate students
Discovering services, resources and perks reserved for grad students only
Knowing when and how to seek in-depth assistance from Concordia subject specialists
Using specialized and subject-specific resources, and getting started with lit reviews
Optimizing access to Concordia resources from on and off campus
Efficiently accessing material within and beyond Concordia's walls
Getting a peek at managing that material via tools like Refworks
Setting up Google Scholar to find Concordia resources
Participant questions and input will be invited throughout the session.
May 10, 2016
10:00am - 12:00pm
Webster Library (LB-322)

2016-05-06
Grad Pro Skills: Engineering & Computer Science Graduate Research Essentials
http://gradstudies.concordia.ca/gradproskills/workshops/workshop/GPRM238
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Apr_2016_12:16:21_EDT
This 90
minute workshop will focus on introducing you to Engineering Village,
a sophisticated discovery platform for current and past engineering & computer
science literature tracked in databases such as Compendex and INSPEC.
Other important engineering resources will also be highlighted.
The workshop will cover how to use Engineering Village to find articles and
conference papers in your field, track research in particular journals or by
specific authors and monitor new research output going forward. We will also
show you briefly how what you learn here can be applied to other resources.
May 6, 2016
9:30 - 11:00am
Webster Library (LB-322)
]]>

19 Apr 2016 12:15:20 EDT
2016-05-04
Grad Pro Skills: Citations and Bibliographies Simplified
http://gradstudies.concordia.ca/gradproskills/workshops/workshop/GPRM236
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Apr_2016_12:15:20_EDT
In this hands-on workshop you will learn how to use RefWorks, a web-based
tool that you can use to organize the references you find in library catalogues and databases,
insert citations in your papers, and prepare bibliographies or reference lists quickly and
effectively, in a wide variety of citation styles (e.g. APA, MLA, Chicago, et cetera). We will
also discuss how to integrate RefWorks with Microsoft Word using RefWorks' Write'n-Cite tool, and
how to share your RefWorks folders and citations (e.g., for collaborative projects or to
disseminate reading lists). No experience with RefWorks is necessary.
May 5, 2016
1:00 - 3:00pm
Webster Library (LB-322)

2016-04-29
Concordia University Libraries' 14th Annual Research Forum
/about/staff/forum/index.php
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i20_Apr_2016_12:16:22_EDT
Since 2002, Concordia's Library Research Forum has provided librarians, archivists, graduate students, teaching faculty, and information professionals with an opportunity to describe and promote their completed or in-progress research, practical case studies or projects. The Forum also provides a venue for researchers to seek suggestions for enhancing their research interests, to identify potential new partners for projects, to test the effectiveness of their undertakings, and to promote research in academic libraries.
April 29, 2016
9:15am - 4:45pm
Loyola Jesuit Hall and Conference Centre, Loyola Campus

23 Feb 2016 10:32:28 EDT
2016-03-19
Traces, Marie Ségolène Brault]]>
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i23_Feb_2016_10:32:28_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i23_Feb_2016_10:32:28_EST
Traces
Feb 18 - Mar 18, 2016
Marie Ségolène C. Brault
BFA student, Studio Arts
Marie Ségolène Brault's practice investigates ideas of personal mythology, rituals and archives through drawing, sculpture, performance and video installations.
She graduated with a BA in Creative Writing from Concordia University where she is now finishing her BFA in Studio Arts, specializing in Intermedia Cyberarts.
Her work has been featured in Poetry is Dead Magazine, Ssissterss, DRY MAGAZINE and NAKID Magazine and her book Proprioception (2015) has recently been published by Book Label. She has participated in several group exhibits, in spaces such as the City Bird Gallery (NYC), Vox Populi (Philadelphia) and the Gallerie Pangée (Montreal).

http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Feb_2016_13:45:26_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Feb_2016_13:45:26_EST
LB2 Bishop St. side will close on February 22 for renovations.
We apologize for the inconvenience.
The Reference Desk will be set up on LB2 Mackay St. side on February 22.
The north staircase will open to users on February 22 – at which time access to the south staircase will be closed.
Express Stations and DPrint machines will be relocated to LB3 Mackay St. side and will not be accessible between February 22 and 28.
Students are encouraged to use DPrint machines on other floors and on LB1.
Service will resume on February 29.
Computer workstations are now located on LB3 (India and France rooms) and on LB4 (Bishop side).

7 Dec 2015 12:38:18 EDT
New discovery search and library home page launched
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i7_Dec_2015_12:38:18_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i7_Dec_2015_12:38:18_EST
We've redesigned our home page based on feedback received in our 2014 usability study and in the .
Here's a summary of the changes:
The new discovery search – a valuable tool for undergraduates searching on a topic as well as interdisciplinary researchers—is prominent on the home page
A search box and link to the library catalogue is secondary to the discovery search
Top library services are highlighted in the blue bar: book a study room, course reserves, citation guides & RefWorks, databases by subject, ejournals, and how to connect from off-campus
MetaFind has been replaced by the new discovery search
Links to additional resources (reference, other collections and Spectrum) are available under the “Find” tab
Dynamically generated opening hours for Webster Library, Vanier Library and Grey Nuns Reading Room are listed on the home page
News items now have images; notices and events are listed separately
Desktop computer availability at both Webster and Vanier Libraries has been added to the laptop and tablet availability on the home page
New main navigation puts all help-related content under the same Help & how-to tab, with additional tabs for Find (links to all resources), Locations & hours, and About the Library
See also:

2015-12-18
Text messaging service pilot project, Dec. 1-18 in Webster Library
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i27_Nov_2015_15:38:18_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i27_Nov_2015_15:38:18_EST
The Libraries are piloting a text message service at Webster Library from December 1- December 18, 2015. The service will be offered Monday to Thursday, 1pm to 9pm, and Fridays, 1pm to 5pm. The primary goal of the service is to provide users who are being disrupted by other user's behaviours (ex: speaking in silent areas) with a method to communicate the disruption to Library staff. Just text your location and the problem to 514-245-2326.
The Libraries' study hall monitors will respond to each text message to inform the sender that they are on their way to help. Once they arrive, the monitors will ask the user causing the disruption to comply with the Library's Code of Conduct.
At the conclusion of the pilot period, the project will be evaluated. If it is deemed a success, a recommendation may be made to extend the project.
]]>

New Discovery Search and library home page launching on Dec. 7
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i27_Nov_2015_16:38:18_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i27_Nov_2015_16:38:18_EST
You asked, we listened!
The #1 reason why students visit the library's website is to find articles and we are planning on making that task much easier. Our , which has been in beta since September, will be fully launched and featured prominently on the library website's home page on December 7.
The
allows you to search both the library's physical and digital collections at the same time and receive results in a single list. The
is best described as a topic search which will expose you to a large variety of library print and subscription materials related to your topic. Search results include relevant materials found in the library catalogue, plus a large proportion of our subscription database articles in full-text, ebooks, images, and more!
The redesigned home page features:
Icons linking to top library services, including links to book a group study room and access course reserves
Specialized information for undergraduate students, graduate students and faculty
Dynamically generated library hours
Events listing and images for What's New
Desktop computer availability at both Vanier and Webster Libraries
.
See also:

Seeking nominations for staff award
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i16_Nov_2015_15:38:18_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i16_Nov_2015_15:38:18_EST
Here is an opportunity to recognize the good service you have received from the Libraries.
Nominations are now being sought for the . This award was established to encourage and reward staff currently working for Concordia Libraries whose commitment and professionalism reflect the values exemplified by Freda Otchere.
This award is made possible through the generous gift of Dr. Dan Otchere, Associate Professor of Economics at Concordia University, who created the Freda Otchere Endowment Fund in 2010 in honour of his wife. From 1970 to 2004, Freda Otchere served the Concordia University Libraries as cataloguer and Head of Database Maintenance. Her exemplary service to the Concordia community is warmly remembered, and provides the model by which nominees are identified.
Anyone may nominate a library employee for this award.
See also:
Library staff September 2015

New Archives and Special Collections catalogue launched
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i30_Oct_2015_15:38:18_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i30_Oct_2015_15:38:18_EDT
A joint project between Concordia University's Archives and the Libraries' Special Collections, this shared catalogue leverages access to our archives so that students, faculty, staff, researchers and the general public can use them to understand Concordia's role in the development of Montreal and the world. With this shared catalogue, scholars around the world now have free and easy access to descriptions of our special collections on topics like Montreal, Quebec and Canadian history, genocide, the Holocaust, the Irish in Montreal, Jazz in Montreal, visual arts, or communication studies.
There are over 3000 descriptions available online, including 1500 photos and archival documents from our 400 institutional archival fonds and 145 research archives. You can access the catalogue here: .
Some highlights include the archives of , the archives of Montreal poet , scripts from the television series Law & Order in the archives of Emmy-winning director and Concordia alumnus , and the many audio recordings of the .
Chris James and Alex Mills (Special Collections Curator) examine a rare book in the Libraries' Special Collections.

Open Access Week at Concordia, Oct. 19-23
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Oct_2015_20:11:18_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Oct_2015_20:11:18_EDT
October 19-23 marks International Open Access Week.
Open Access means free, immediate, online access to the results of scholarly research, and the right to use and re-use those results as needed. Open Access Week is a global event, now entering its 8th year, focused on promoting Open Access as a new norm in scholarship and research.
Concordia established itself as a Canadian leader in support for Open Access with the 2010
encouraging faculty and students to make their research freely available in , Concordia's Open Access Research repository, or another Open Access venue. Spectrum currently holds more than 13,000 items, including peer-reviewed articles, book sections and conference presentations submitted by Concordia faculty, as well as graduate theses.
For more information about Open Access at Concordia and around the world, see Concordia Libraries' .
Happy Open Access Week!
Follow us on Twitter as we tweet daily this week about #OpenAccess:
Read more about Spectrum and Open Access at Concordia:

Time: 9 a.m. – 5 p.m.
Where: LB2 (main floor of the Webster Library)
We're looking for students with a keen interest in visual, information or usability design to provide feedback on our digital collections discovery module.
What's the digital collections discovery module? It's the software interface behind large touch screens we're designing for you to explore the Libraries' rich digital collection of resources. From images, audio recordings, articles, essays and videos—you'll soon have our collections available at your fingertips as part of the Webster Library Transformation.
So, take a moment and tell us what you think. The prototype will be on display for you to provide feedback at the main entrance of the Webster Library. ]]>

2015-10-18
Exhibition: Tripping Hazard: Urban Clay 2015
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i16_Sep_2015_10:26:55_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i16_Sep_2015_10:26:55_EDT
Date: Sept 8 – Oct 17, 2015
In 2015 work from the Urban Clay (Ceramics 398b) course occupied all sorts of spaces at Concordia -  walls and pillars, in the middle of the floor, under escalators, throughout stairwells, on windows and in trees to name a few. These projects were temporary public artworks comprised of cast ceramic multiples. The works tend to play off of what already exists in the space and bring a new experience to the public.
Several students used this caution sign near their work, just in case the passerby did not notice it. It turns out that ‘tripping’ is a good metaphor for the way the public encounters Urban Clay projects, as they interrupt and disrupt what we are used to and jolt us into paying attention to the city we inhabit. ]]>

04 Sep 2015 13:15:27 EDT
2015-10-01
Welcome to the Libraries, from Guylaine Beaudry, University Librarian
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i04_Sep_2015_13:15:27_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i04_Sep_2015_13:15:27_EDT
Dear Concordia students,
It’s a great pleasure for me to welcome you to Concordia University and to its Libraries!
In an unprecedented effort to answer your longstanding requests for additional and quality study spaces, over the past month we’ve been working simultaneously on three major projects: They include the Webster Library Transformation, the Vanier Library renovations, and last but not least, the conversion of the former Grey Nuns Chapel and adjacent rooms into the magnificent Grey Nuns Reading Room and group study rooms.  The Vanier and Grey Nuns projects were recently delivered and the Webster Library Transformation will be completed by fall 2017.
The
is a four-phase project.  Once completed, the overall project will increase study space by 27 per cent and study seats by 114 per cent. What’s more, the plan includes 12 different types of study areas — ranging from dedicated space for graduate students to a zero-noise room and collaborative study spaces equipped with the latest learning technologies.  Phase 1 of the Webster Library Transformation (LB3 East and 2 classrooms on LB3 West) will be completed by the end of September 2015 and work has already begun on Phase 2 (LB5 East and West).
The Webster and Vanier libraries are open 24 hours/7 days-a-week and both libraries now have a self-service Course Reserve Room.  The self-service facility allows you to browse the collection by course, to peruse and copy the material you select and finally, to borrow the items you need by using the self-checkout station.  You also have access to
and self-serve
stations.
Discover your Libraries’ rich online world by visiting our .  It’s your gateway to world class research resources – over 500 databases of research literature covering .  Don’t hesitate to ask for help as you navigate through these resources. You can talk to a
by chat or email, and of course by telephone or in-person at one of our information desks.
We’re eager to hear from you. If you would like to share a suggestion or voice a concern, please visit our blog-style . We aim to be continually aware of and responsive to your research and study needs. In fact, many of the Libraries’ great services, such as the ability to
and tablets, Montreal’s first 24/7 , and the self-serve
textbooks and readings were only made possible by your suggestions and support!
Thank you for your engagement, your constructive contributions and to all of you, good luck with your 2015-16 academic year!
Guylaine Beaudry, Ph.D.University Librarian]]>

Please note that RefWorks will be unavailable from approximately 12noon to 5pm on Wednesday June 17, 2015.
The service interruption is necessary as Concordia is migrating its RefWorks service from a Canadian server to a U.S. based server, as the Canadian service will be discontinued.
For more information, please see our . See especially the section "What will change? How will I be affected?".
For help with any questions or issues, please contact Jared Wiercinski ( or 514 848-2424 extension 7726.)]]>

2015-06-09
Vanier Library Exhibition: Comfort and Pleasure: English Porcelain Tea Cups c1900-1935
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i9_Jun_2015_9:08:47_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i9_Jun_2015_9:08:47_EDT
Tea is many things to many people. For some, it is a source of caffeine consumed for a quick boost, for many other it can be a source of comfort.  It is a ritual with very specific rules to follow; the temperature of the water; the blend of tea – in a bag vs. loose leaf; the construction of the teapot and shape of the cup. Every step is carefully prescribed and differs for each individual.  Do you add the milk before you pour or after? Or not at all? George Orwell had eleven steps for the perfect cup of tea and every step essential.1
This display of fine porcelain tea cups at the Vanier Library highlights the years 1900-1935 when new styles and shapes were influenced by the art trends of the time. In this display you will see many examples of the richly decorated imari style as well as some in the art deco and art nouveau styles.  Most of the cups in the display were manufactured in Staffordshire, England by T.C. Wild &Sons Ltd. later known by the brand "Royal Albert".
You can see all Orwell’s rules
or in the essay,  "A nice cup of tea" in The Collected Essays, Journalism and Letters of George Orwell, Volume 3, 1943-45 located on the 3rd Floor of Webster Library:  PR 6029 R8A16 1968
]]>

2015-06-17
RefWorks June 17, 2015 migration to U.S. based server
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i13_May_2015_13:59:41_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i13_May_2015_13:59:41_EDT
Migration to a U.S. based server
Concordia Libraries’ RefWorks service, a voluntary service, will move from being hosted on a Canadian server to a U.S. based server as the Canadian service will be discontinued.
After the migration, your citations, files (if any), e-mail address and name will be stored on a U.S. server and subject to current and future legislation applicable in the U.S., including the USA PATRIOT Act, that allows U.S. authorities to access the personal information that you provide.
Technical changes
The migration will cause minor changes that include:
The URL (i.e. web address) of the login page will change, as will the URL of any shared accounts or folders.
Any RefWorks users who use the Write-n-Cite plug-in will need to download and install a new version. The plug-in will have a new name: ProQuest for Word.
Once the migration is complete, some users will receive an email that provides a new login name (which will be the email address used to create your account).
For more information about these changes, please see our information page, available at:
Time and date of the migration
The move is scheduled to occur on June 17, 2015 at 12 noon and will last approximately 5 hours. RefWorks will be unavailable during that time.
Opting out
If you would like to opt out of having your account and data migrated to the RefWorks U.S. server, we can help you to export your data and delete your account ahead of the migration.
To opt out, or if you have any questions, please contact me by email or telephone at
or 514 848-2424 extension 7726.

2015-04-17
Hounded by exam stress? Meet one of our pet therapy dogs
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i4_Mar_2015_11:12:10_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i4_Mar_2015_11:12:10_EST
Vanier Library, April 13th and 15th, 2015 from 11:30-1:30
Webster Library, April 14th and 16th, 2015 from 11:30-1:30
Exam period can be stressful. And while there are a lot of ways to cope, is there anything more relaxing than the company of a furry, friendly animal?
On April 13th and 15th, the Vanier Library, on the Loyola Campus and on April 14th and 16th the Webster Library, on the Sir George Williams Campus will welcome several pet-therapy dogs from the Blue Ribbon Canine Centre. They’ll be on hand to help students de-stress and relax.
The visit will take place from 11:30-1:30 p.m. outside of Room VL-101 for Vanier and in the LB-201 area at Webster.
We welcomed the pet-therapy dogs last April and similar sessions have been used successfully at McGill University; the University of California, Berkeley; the University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign; the University of Wisconsin; and Yale University to help reduce anxiety and lift moods.
Photo Credit: Sleek Photography
Meet Brandy the Shetland sheepdog
Among the canines on hand for the session will be Brandy, a Shetland sheepdog.
Along with her fellow pet-therapy dogs, Brandy will be waiting for you in the library. Brandy has met many people during her eight-year career, and is a proud founding member of Blue Ribbon Therapy Dogs.
As a performance dog who has participated in many dog-sport trials, she understands the pressure of exams.
She looks forward to her visit to Concordia, and hopes to brighten everyone's day.
All of the dogs have been vaccinated and will be on four-foot leashes.
For more information about the Blue Ribbon Canine Centre, visit: ]]>

Webster Library Exhibition: LetterForm[s]
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i2_Apr_2015_13:33:55_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i2_Apr_2015_13:33:55_EDT
Atrium area – 2nd floor  April 2 – 15, 2015
Creating these letterforms helped students from DART331 [Words in Space] develop an awareness and understanding of the design of letterforms by observing and recording them in a context of public lettering and then creating a 3D model of 2 selected characters. Students engaged with the aesthetics and cultural contexts of the typography in its public environment and based their rendering on a typeface of their choice found from a source of public lettering.

March 26: APA writing and reference style workshop
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i12_Mar_2015_11:07:58_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i12_Mar_2015_11:07:58_EDT
Why attend? Do you need to prepare an assignment using APA style? In this workshop, you will be introduced to some of the guidelines provided in the Publication Manual of the American Psychological Association. Topics covered will include how to keep track of sources that you find during your research process, how to properly cite sources in your paper, and some basics of setting up your APA document including the Running Head and the Title Page.

2015-03-10 10:00:00
March 10: Memory and Commemoration: The Azrieli Holocaust Collection at Thirty
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i16_Feb_2015_12:50:15_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i16_Feb_2015_12:50:15_EST
The Concordia University Libraries invite you to attend “Memory and Commemoration: The Azrieli Holocaust Collection at Thirty,” a one day symposium in Montreal, Quebec, on Tuesday, March 10, 2015, marking the thirtieth anniversary of the creation of what is now one of the largest collections in North America of research materials on the Holocaust. The Collection was established in 1984 by Montreal businessman and philanthropist David Azrieli, CM, CQ (1922-2014), whose parents, brother, and sister died in the Holocaust. More information on the Collection is available here: .
The symposium begins at 2 p.m. in Room 767 of the Hall Building (7th floor, 1455 de Maisonneuve Blvd West) and will feature a panel of emerging and established Holocaust scholars from Concordia, Texas A&M, Michigan, and Graz, followed by a keynote by Debórah Dwork, the Rose Professor of Holocaust History at Clark University. The event concludes with a reception hosted by the Azrieli Foundation and the Consulate General of the German Federal Republic, Montreal.
The event is free and open to the public and the full program is available here:
Many sponsors have made this event possible including: Social Sciences and Humanities Research Council of Canada; the Azrieli Foundation; Austrian Embassy, Ottawa; Consulate General of the German Federal Republic, Montreal; Concordia University Office of the Vice-President, Research & Graduate Studies, Faculty of Arts & Sciences, Department of History, Montreal Institute for Genocide and Human Rights Studies, Department of Political Science, Department of Religion, Azrieli Institute of Israel Studies, Concordia Institute for Jewish Studies, Mel Hoppenheim School of Cinema; and the McGill University Department of Jewish Studies.
For more information, contact:
Geoffrey Little Curator of the Azrieli Holocaust Collection ]]>

13 Feb 2015 13:49:39 EST
Linda Quartz, recipient of the 2014 Freda Otchere Staff Recognition Award
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i13_Feb_2015_13:49:39_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i13_Feb_2015_13:49:39_EST
The
was established "to encourage and reward staff currently working for Concordia Libraries whose commitment and professionalism reflect the values exemplified by Freda Otchere".  The award, which carries with it a single lump sum payment of $650, is made possible through the generous gift of Dr. Dan Otchere, Associate Professor of Economics at Concordia University, who created the Freda Otchere Endowment Fund in 2010 in honour of his wife. From 1970 to 2004, Freda Otchere served the Concordia University Libraries as cataloguer and Head of Database Maintenance. Her exemplary service to the Concordia community is warmly remembered, and provides the model by which nominees are identified. The award is made annually by the University Librarian on the recommendation of the Staff Recognition Award Committee.
Linda Quartz is the recipient of the 2014 Freda Otchere Staff Recognition Award. Congratulations, Linda!
We would like to thank all of the people who made nominations and the members of the Staff Recognition Award Committee: Joseph Capano, Anna Michetti, Karen Mullett, David Thirlwall and Luigina Vileno. Here is a statement from the Chair of the committee, David Thirlwall, about this year’s award recipient:
Linda is “appreciated by her colleagues for her candor and compassion.” She is known for “creating a sense of community and belonging”. A prime example in 2014 is the leadership she showed in organizing a welcome for the Collections Services staff who moved into Vanier Library during the summer. This was a big change for the group, many of whom had been serving downtown for over 20 years. This example is one of many initiatives Linda took to organize memorable social events.
“This concern for staff well-being”, says one nominator, “also extends to students”. Linda was instrumental in planning and delivering the renowned
to address the stress that so many students are enduring. A nominator explained that “the idea had been discussed by several people before, but Linda was the one who finally made it happen”. She made herculean efforts in order to bring this idea to life. Her actions brought unprecedented attention to Vanier Library, including .
With these examples in mind, it is readily seen that Linda has made wonderful contributions to the University.  Her actions have brought support to the Concordia community, and have upheld the Concordia brand which promotes collegiality, respect, and attention to our students.
Linda made these exciting achievements over and above her usual exemplary work in the Vanier Library Media & Document Delivery unit. On a day to day basis, she presents “an example of equity, honesty and helpfulness in all of her interactions with students, co-workers and administrators”. “She volunteers to take on extra tasks”. She is “the person who helps move an idea from talk to action”.]]>

Webster Library Exhibition: Articulating Spaces
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i7_Jan_2015_12:56:46_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i7_Jan_2015_12:56:46_EST
Atrium 2nd floor,  Jan 6 – 30, 2015
D.J. Thompson. Tradewinds: My Voyage.Intaglio prints on Japanese paper. Accordion structure.2.75 x 2.75  x 0.75”. (2014)
The works in this exhibition include artists’ books and boxes produced by Concordia University Studio Arts students. The individual bookworks highlight how artists explore the space of the book structure to interrogate traditional forms. In the boxes, students from print media, ceramics, fibres, etc. have worked in collaboration to build on the tradition of games and match boxes. Incorporating personal, historical, and  mythological stories and concepts, these works intermingle images and/or texts that speak volumes.
Curated by Melinda Reinhart, Visual Arts Librarian

Concordia University Libraries Christmas Auction Committee is holding its annual Christmas Auction on Thursday December 11, 2014.  Every year the Library Staff of Concordia University Libraries hold an auction to raise funds for charitable organizations in our community.  It’s our Silver Anniversary!  This is the 25th year that we are holding our fund raising Auction to benefit:
Auberge Madeleine, Can Serve Foundation, Chez Doris, CODE (Canadian Organization for Development through Education), Concordia University Centre for the Arts in Human Development (CAHD), Multi-Faith Chaplaincy and Financial Aids and Awards, Dans la Rue, the Gazette Christmas Fund, Operation Eyesight Universal, OXFAM, Sun Youth, and the Women's Centre of Montreal.
The event will be held in the J.A. De Sève Cinema, LB-125 in the Library Building (J. W. McConnell Building) at 1400 de Maisonneuve Blvd. West, Montreal QC H3G 1M8 (between MacKay Street and Bishop Street).  The event will be from 12:00 pm to 2:00 pm on Thursday December 11, 2014.  Food will be sold.  Auctionable items have included signed hockey sticks, caps & t-shirts from the Montreal Canadiens, books, CDs, jams, paintings, jewelry, cosmetics, and gift certificates to downtown restaurants.  Many varied items are part of our annual Auction.

2015-01-07
Webster Library Exhibition: Playing the Jester | Urban Clay Projects
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i26_Nov_2014_14:04:30_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i26_Nov_2014_14:04:30_EST
Atrium 2nd floor
Nov. 20, 2014 – Jan. 5, 2015
Glen Adamson describes craft as a ‘cunning jester’ in the post disciplinary art world. He describes craft as cleverly poised to move fluidly through the boundaries that surround art and design, escaping the art world easier than art, going into the factory and coming out again into any kind of space. In the space of the city, students from the Urban Clay class at Concordia use ceramics to play the jester in shifting identity between art, design and even technology through temporary site-specific public art installations on the urban campus.
Curated by Professor Linda Swanson

Hounded by exam stress? Meet one of our pet therapy dogs
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i11_Nov_2014_13:09:39_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i11_Nov_2014_13:09:39_EST
Vanier Library, November 25 and 27, from 11:00 to 2:00 p.m.
Exam period can be stressful. And while there are a lot of ways to cope, is there anything more relaxing than the company of a furry, friendly animal?
On November 25 and 27, the Vanier Library, on the Loyola Campus, will welcome several pet-therapy dogs from the Blue Ribbon Canine Centre. They’ll be on hand to help students de-stress and relax.
The visit will take place from 11:00 to 2:00 p.m. outside of Room VL-101.
We welcomed the pet-therapy dogs last April and similar sessions have been used successfully at McGill University; the University of California, Berkeley; the University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign; the University of Wisconsin; and Yale University to help reduce anxiety and lift moods.
Photo Credit: Sleek Photography
Meet Brandy the Shetland sheepdog
Among the canines on hand for the session will be Brandy, a Shetland sheepdog.
Along with her fellow pet-therapy dogs, Brandy will be waiting for you in the library. Brandy has met many people during her eight-year career, and is a proud founding member of Blue Ribbon Therapy Dogs.
As a performance dog who has participated in many dog-sport trials, she understands the pressure of exams.
She looks forward to her visit to Concordia, and hopes to brighten everyone's day.
All of the dogs have been vaccinated and will be on four-foot leashes.
For more information about the Blue Ribbon Canine Centre, visit: ]]>

We’re very pleased to announce that on Wednesday, October 22, Concordia's Board of Governors approved the Webster Library Transformation project.
This project will address a longstanding need for more student study space in response to the almost tripling of our student population since the library first opened in 1992. Study seats will increase by 114% and the quality and variety of spaces will improve. .]]>

Webster Library Exhibition: The Library of Performing Rights
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i28_Oct_2014_16:56:24_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i28_Oct_2014_16:56:24_EDT
Atrium 2nd floor
Oct 17 – Nov 17, 2014
The Library of Performing Rights is a unique resource containing publications, videos, DVDs, brochures, digital and web-based initiatives submitted by artists, activists and academics  from around the world that examine the intersections of performance and social justice. The Library was created to bring together a body of materials, documentation and evidence that both archive the remains of performance-related interventions and stimulate performance and human rights experimentation.
Curated by Joanna Donehower, Jessica Rae Alley, Véronique Guimond-Payette in collaboration with Alicia Fleas Segura and Julian Duarte.
