28 Oct 2014 17:21:07 EDT
November 6: Azrieli Holocaust Collection Open House
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i28_Oct_2014_17:21:07_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i28_Oct_2014_17:21:07_EDT
in the Concordia University Libraries is marking its 30th anniversary in 2014-15 with a series of public events including an open house and a colloquium.
On Thursday, November 6 from 3pm to 7pm, members of the Concordia community and the public are invited to an open house at the Vanier Library (7141 Sherbrooke St W.). This event is being held as part of Holocaust Education Week. Recent acquisitions from the collection (approximately 60 items) will be on display, including rare acquisitions like anti-Semitic materials produced in Europe and North America before and after the Nazi’s came to power in 1933; reports by Allied governments and non-governmental groups describing growing violence against Jews in Germany and as well as the scope of Nazi atrocities, and post-war publications illustrating the scale and enormity of the Holocaust. Recently published secondary works will also be on display. Geoffrey Little, the collection's curator, will give a guided tour of materials at 4pm and 6pm. All are welcome.
On Tuesday, March 10 the Libraries will hold a colloquium on the theme of the Holocaust and Memory in the D.B. Clarke Theatre. Christopher Browning, emeritus professor of history at UNC Chapel Hill and a respected Holocaust scholar, is a confirmed speaker. More details will be announced shortly.
The Azrieli Holocaust Collection was established in 1984 with an endowment from Montreal businessman and philanthropist David Azrieli, CM, CQ (1922-2014), whose parents, brother, and sister died in the Holocaust. Today the collection is the largest and most specialized in Canada on the history of the Holocaust and Nazi Germany, the history of anti-Semitism, and the history of Jewish-Christian relations in the 19th and 20th centuries. It also documents the immeasurable impact of the Holocaust on post-Holocaust life, thought, and culture with special emphasis on Canada and the United States.
The collection contains approximately 8,500 titles from almost every discipline and includes rare books and ephemera from the 1920s, 30s, and 40s; digitized primary sources; microfilm collections of government records and war crimes trials; documentaries and feature films; survivor memoirs and diaries; and secondary texts. The Azrieli Holocaust Collection is an invaluable resource for Concordia students and faculty as well as for the broader community.
For more information, contact Geoffrey Little ( / 514-848-2424 x 7748)

14 Oct 2014 13:22:10 EDT
Call for papers: Colloquium Celebrating the Azrieli Holocaust Collection
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i14_Oct_2014_13:22:10_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i14_Oct_2014_13:22:10_EDT
Memory and Commemoration: A Celebration of the Azrieli Holocaust Collection
10 March 2015
Concordia University
Montreal, Quebec
The
was established in 1984 with an endowment from Montreal philanthropist and businessman David J. Azrieli, CM, CQ (1922-2014), whose parents, sister, and brother were killed during the Holocaust. It is now one of the most important specialized collections in North America for research and teaching on the Holocaust and the history of anti-Semitism. It also documents the history of Nazi Germany, the history of Jewish-Christian relations in the nineteenth and twentieth centuries, and the impact of the Holocaust on post-Holocaust life, thought, and art with emphasis on Canada and the United States.
To mark the Collection’s thirtieth anniversary, which coincides with the seventieth anniversary of the liberation of the death camps and the end of the Second World War, Concordia University is organizing a one day colloquium in Montreal on 10 March 2015. Christopher R. Browning, the Frank Porter Graham Professor Emeritus Professor of History at the University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill, is a confirmed speaker. We seek to gather scholars who have written about and studied the Holocaust from the vantage points of memory, commemoration, and culture. We also hope to publish selected contributions.
Proposals for papers, including those from emerging or junior scholars, are invited. We welcome proposals that address aspects of the creation of Holocaust memory through historical scholarship, museum exhibitions, memorials and monuments, literature, film, or popular culture. Proposals should be no more than 300 words and should include a CV. Materials should be sent in one file, preferably as a PDF, to Geoffrey Little (). The deadline for submissions is Tuesday, 18 November 2014. Applicants will be notified in December 2014. Funding may be available for presenters. ]]>

UPDATED: CLUES catalogue, databases, and COLOMBO unavailable all day Mon. Aug. 18
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i13_Aug_2014_12:45:29_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i13_Aug_2014_12:45:29_EDT
Update (as of 6pm): Thank you for your continued patience while we get our systems back online. You may notice that some services are intermittently available, but all systems are not yet available. We will post an update when we are completely back online.
There will be a scheduled library system service interruption to allow for important upgrades taking place on August 18. We expect to be operational by the morning of Tuesday, August 19.
During this migration, the library system will be completely shut down, and most services will be affected, including access to databases, self-checkout machines, COLOMBO interlibrary loans, and CLUES library catalogue. Our laptop and tablet lending service will also be unavailable.
We ask for your patience and cooperation during this time. We apologize for any inconvenience this may cause.]]>

Collections Services Division moves to the Vanier Library
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i10_Jun_2014_15:55:51_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i10_Jun_2014_15:55:51_EDT
On June 12, 2014, the Collection Services Division will move from the Webster Library on the downtown campus to the third floor of Vanier Library on the Loyola campus.
The move will improve overall efficiency of the Concordia Libraries and the quality of our spaces in response to the needs of our growing student population.
Collections Services is responsible for ordering, cataloguing, managing and assessing books, journals, media and electronic resources.
For more details, read the Vanier Library Renovations FAQs

26 May 2014 11:15:52 EDT
2014-07-04
Webster Library Exhibition: Art as Books
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i26_May_2014_11:15:52_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i26_May_2014_11:15:52_EDT
Atrium 2nd floor, May 17 – July 4, 2014
Art as Books
This site-specific exhibition  tends to relate to the artistic process of creation and its own archive. Each of the four vitrines are divided in two different forms of artistic editions. One is sealed, untouchable because of the immobility in both the boxes they are in and the space where they are shown. The other is series of sketched edited books, intended to show the process for potential projects. These two bodies of work bridge together the notions of artistic legacy and the finality of a work of art. Are books the final result of an art work? Are sketches meant to be shown? What is art?
Timothée Messeiller, MFA student in Studio Arts, Concordia University. Estelle Bourdet, Artist in residence.

Webster Library Exhibition: Multiplicities
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i29_Apr_2014_18:55:31_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i29_Apr_2014_18:55:31_EDT

Multiplicities

Webster Library Exhibition: Commonplace Books for Drawing
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i11_Feb_2014_15:19:58_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i11_Feb_2014_15:19:58_EST
Commonplace Books for Drawing
Date: Feb 7 – Feb 26, 2014
Location: Webster Library 2nd floor Atrium
These commonplace books were compiled and made by Art History 356 students as a method to investigate the nature of drawing, both as a material object and an activity. The commonplace book is a Renaissance invention, used to collect, compile, and classify passages, or facts encountered in books, or in nature. The gathering of material could be used for future arguments, speeches, or texts, with indexing easing the retrieval of material. (Professor Charles Gagnon)
Students:
Madelyne Beckles
Ellen Belshaw
Victoria Byron
Meagan Coleman
Ellis Green

18 Dec 2013 18:21:13 EST
Improved access to the library for Moodle users
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i18_Dec_2013_18:21:13_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i18_Dec_2013_18:21:13_EST
A new Library Resources block now appears in Moodle. The goal of the block is to improve student access to library collections and services by promotion through Moodle, a starting point for many students engaged in coursework.
The Library Resources block automatically displays on the side of all Moodle course sites, adjacent to course content. Content within the block is generated dynamically, and is tailored to the specific Moodle course that the student has logged into. The Library Resources block provides convenient access to course textbooks, librarian recommended research databases and journals, the library catalogue, and more.
Here is an example of what the Library Resources block looks like:
For more information, or to provide feeback, please visit our .

http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i19_Nov_2013_12:28:28_EST
The library is looking at installing technologies to support collaboration and will be testing equipment in the next few months.
As a trial project, we have set up Media:scape in the main corridor by the entrance to the library. Media:scape is furniture and technology integrated together with dual screens to allow you to share information from your tablets and laptops. It was generously lent to the library by a supplier for testing, so we encourage you to be gentle with it so that we may return it in good condition. Connectors to plug in Apple devices are available for lending at the Circulation Desk.

The Concordia University Libraries' Annual Christmas Auction will be held on Thursday, December 5, 2013 from 12:00 - 2:00 p.m. in the J. A. De Sève Cinema, LB-125 in the Library Building (J. W. McConnell Building).
Proceeds go to benefit charitable organizations in the community as well as Concordia departments such as the Concordia University Centre for the Arts in Human Development (CAHD), the Multi-Faith Chaplaincy, and the Financial Aid and Awards Office.
The entrance fee is $2 or a raffle ticket. Food will be available for sale.
At previous events, auctionable items have included everything from signed hockey sticks, caps and t-shirts from the Montreal Canadiens to signed footballs from the Alouettes. APA style workshop
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i12_Nov_2013_13:15:40_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i12_Nov_2013_13:15:40_EST
Why attend? Do you need to prepare an assignment using APA style? In this workshop, you will be introduced to some of the guidelines provided in the Publication Manual of the American Psychological Association. Topics covered will include how to keep track of sources that you find during your research process, how to properly cite sources in your paper, and some basics of setting up your APA document including the Running Head and the Title Page.

Scoop on Scopus Day, Fri., Nov. 1
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i25_Oct_2013_16:39:00_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i25_Oct_2013_16:39:00_EDT
Join us for a Scoop on Scopus Day at Concordia University!
Date: November 1st, 2013
Location: Webster Library, LB-203
is an abstract and citation database containing both peer-reviewed research literature and quality web sources. With over 21,000 titles from more than 5,000 international publishers, Scopus covers scientific, technical, medical and social sciences fields as well as the arts and humanities.
On Friday November 1, publisher representatives will be conducting two Scopus workshops in conjunction with Concordia University Libraries. Join us for one, or both sessions, in room LB-203 of the Webster Library!
Breakfast Session (10 am): Making the Most of Scopus
Attend if you need to know …
What is the most important article in your field?
How many times has your article been cited? Or an article written by your friend/advisor/colleague?
How many Humanities titles are covered in Scopus? How many books?
How to conduct a literature search that crosses multiple disciplines (for example, engineering, computer science, and environmental science)?
Lunch Session (12 pm): Scopus and Bibliometrics
Attend if you need to know…
How to track article output, citation counts and author collaboration around the world at the individual and institution level.
How to clean up author profiles in Scopus and send details and publication lists to ORCID.
How to analyze research output by subject area, paper type, source title, institution and co-author network.
How to calculate h-index, citation count and co-author network for individual researchers.

Celebrate Open Access Week, Oct. 21-27
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i21_Oct_2013_16:42:12_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i21_Oct_2013_16:42:12_EDT
Open Access means free, immediate, online access to the results of scholarly research, and the right to use and re-use those results as needed.
is a global event, now entering its 6th year, focused on promoting Open Access as a new norm in scholarship and research.
Concordia established itself as a Canadian leader in support for Open Access with the 2010
encouraging faculty and students to make their research freely available in , Concordia's Open Access Research repository, or another Open Access venue. Spectrum currently holds more than 10,000 items, including peer-reviewed articles, book sections and conference presentations submitted by Concordia faculty, as well as graduate theses. To read more about the success of Concordia's Open Access repository, check out the recent article about Spectrum in .
For more information about Open Access at Concordia and around the world, see Concordia Libraries' .
Happy Open Access Week!]]>

3 Oct 2013 12:07:26 EDT
Colombo, the Libraries' Interlibrary Loans system, now delivers articles via email!
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i3_Oct_2013_12:07:26_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i3_Oct_2013_12:07:26_EDT
Starting this week, Concordia University Libraries’ Interlibrary Loans Service (ILL) introduces electronic delivery of article requests. Thanks to an upgrade in the Colombo system, shared by all CREPUQ institutions, and changes to the Canadian Copyright Act, you will now receive articles and parts of works via your email, making this well used service more convenient and faster for you.
Some things to know about the new service:
You will receive an email that your article is ready for viewing. The email will contain an access link/URL which will lead to a webpage with a copyright statement. You will be asked to confirm that you have understood the legal uses of the material you requested before proceeding to it.
The article, or part of a work, will be available for downloading and printing via the access link/URL for 5 working days following viewing the document for the first time.
Please note that not all articles can be delivered electronically. In some cases, due to licensing or copyright restrictions, lending libraries may only allow for print copies to be delivered to requesters. In these cases articles will need to be picked up on campus as before.
The Interlibrary Loans
and
webpages now contain information about this service.
If you have any questions contact the .

Public Discussion on the Future of Libraries and Archives in Canada
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i7_Oct_2013_10:27:16_EDT

How important to you are the services of libraries and archives? Here’s an opportunity to be heard.
The Royal Society of Canada has established an expert panel to investigate and report on the status and future of Canada’s libraries and archives.  Our Interim University Librarian, Guylaine Beaudry, will be part of this expert panel. Public consultations are being held across Canada. It’s important for them to hear from Canadians about the value they place on libraries and archives, the services they receive and expect from these institutions, and the ways digital technology is transforming our knowledge universe.
Everyone is welcome.
Date: October 24, 2013, 4-6 pm
Location: Pavillon Roger-Gaudry, M-415, Université de Montréal

A welcome message from Guylaine Beaudry, Interim University Librarian
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i5_Sep_2013_16:51:34_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i5_Sep_2013_16:51:34_EDT
Dear Concordia students,
Here we are at the start of an exciting new year. It’s a great pleasure for me to welcome you to Concordia University – and most particularly to the Libraries!
Be sure to visit your two libraries – the Vanier Library on the Loyola Campus and the Webster Library on the Downtown Campus. They’re yours to explore and enjoy. At both you’ll find a welcoming staff, great facilities, great collections, and a full suite of services.
Open 24 hours/7 days-a-week, your libraries are the premier place for study.  Orange study zones offer you spots where you can study quietly together with classmates and friends. Blue study zones provide a silent refuge for individual reading. Self-serve
facilities are always available.
You will soon discover your Libraries’ rich online world. Check out our
– or the . It’s your gateway to world class research resources – over 500 databases of research literature covering . Don’t hesitate to ask for help in navigating these resources. You can talk to a
by chat or email, and of course by telephone or in-person at the Information Desks.
We at the Libraries are eager to hear from you. If you want to air a concern or offer a suggestion, please try out our blog-style . We want to respond to your research and study needs. It is the suggestions and support of students that have brought about many of the Libraries’ great services – to name just a few: a service for
and tablets, Montreal’s first 24/7 , and self-serve
textbooks and readings!
I invite you to drop in to the Libraries' event on Tuesday October 22 in the LB Atrium, where you can learn about the , and how you the students are making Concordia University Libraries into a national leader in academic library service.
Finally, let me wish you all an enjoyable and successful 2013/2014 year of learning.
Yours truly,
Guylaine Beaudry, Ph.D.Interim University Librarian]]>

2013-10-04
Webster Library Exhibition: Life and Death of the Book
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i6_Sep_2013_10:56:50_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i6_Sep_2013_10:56:50_EDT
Life and Death of the Book
Date: Sept 4 – Oct 3, 2013
Location: Webster Library 2nd floor Atrium south
The featured artists’ books explore the current material, visual and textual aspects of the codex. As a grouping of artworks, the exhibition addresses the following questions: If the book could think, could have feelings, and could respond, how would it? How would it respond to the threat of its own death? If the book came back to life and took on a psychological state of its own, what would that look like?
Curator:  Rachel Harris (Mabel Bee curatorial name)
Artists:
Bianca St Martin
Camille Cléant
Coco-Simone Finken
Gabrielle Gingras
Gustavo Lopez Riveros
Mark Laurin
Neah Kelly
Pauline Johnson]]>

You can now pick up your books on hold at any time of day at Webster
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i26_Aug_2013_15:19:32_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i26_Aug_2013_15:19:32_EDT
At the Webster Library, we’ve placed shelves out in the open for books you requested. Now you can pick up the  books you requested without going to the Circulation Desk. This lets you get your books at any time .
The Public Holds Shelf is located close to the entrance of the Webster Library. Interlibrary loans and audiovisual items are still kept behind the Circulation Desk.
For your privacy, we’ve folded a piece of paper around the spine of the book and added a code for you to identify your books. The code is the first 4 letters of your last name plus the last 3 digits of your ID. When you receive an email that your books are ready for pick-up, you will be emailed this code. Simply locate your books on the shelf and check them out using the self-checkout machine (or at the Circulation Desk).There is no change for books being picked up at the Vanier Library.

(Requests in CLUES)

8 Jul 2013 13:09:29 PDT
Protecting your privacy on library laptops
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i8_Jul_2013_13:09:29_PDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i8_Jul_2013_13:09:29_PDT
Users who borrow a laptop from the Libraries should be aware that all files saved to the laptop will be automatically deleted when the computer is rebooted. So, please do not save your files to our laptops – instead, use a USB key, a cloud based site (e.g., Dropbox or Google Drive), or other option to save the file to an external location. Save frequently so that, in the unlikely event that there is a system crash, you don’t lose your work.
The Libraries made this change to protect the privacy of our users’ files on these shared computers. No files will be viewable by the next patron who borrows the laptop. The laptop will wipe all files on reboot.]]>

DPrint is now available at both Webster and Vanier Libraries
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i24_Jan_2013_13:04:40_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i24_Jan_2013_13:04:40_EST
Both Webster and Vanier Libraries have completely switched over to DPrint. Old printers, photocopiers and debit card loaders are no longer available. At both libraries, all regular and express workstations
(excluding CLUES-only workstations) now have
as the default printing option. It
means that you will be able to print, photocopy, and/or scan and pay with your
Concordia ID. You'll be able to pick up your print job from the DPrint
printer-copier at either library or from any other DPrint printer-copier
on campus.
To use the DPrint
printer-copiers, you need to:
Load money onto your Concordia ID using a DPrint loader* (cash
only),
Log into one of the regular or express workstations,
Send your document to print, and
Go to either a B&W or colour DPrint printer-copier (depending
on your document), swipe your ID and select your document to print.
For more information, see the
Digital Store’s  about
the new Concordia-wide DPrint Printing Service or check out our section on
.
*There are two DPrint cash
loaders located at the downtown campus next to the Digital Boutique (LB-119).
There is one cash loader located at the Loyola Campus in the Vanier Library at
the front counter.]]>

A new tool called “WebPrint” is now available. It allows you to upload a document from wherever you are (even from home) and release the document from any DPrint printer-copier on campus. Just put money your Concordia ID using one of the DPrint loaders* and swipe your Concordia ID card on the DPrint printer-copier to pay for your print job. Here’s the link:
*On the Sir George Williams (downtown) campus, there are 2 DPrint loaders located at the bottom of the stairs by the entrance to the library. On the Loyola Campus, there is 1 DPrint loader located in the Vanier Library by the front counter. ]]>

Journals in Vanier compact shelving now accessible to users
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i29_Nov_2012_10:46:59_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i29_Nov_2012_10:46:59_EST
We’re pleased to announce that journals recently moved to compact shelving units at the Vanier Library are now accessible to users. As part of this year’s , all print journals more than 5 years old (10 years old for fine arts) have been moved to compact shelving units on the ground floor of the Vanier Library on the Loyola campus. This journal move is part of the larger, ongoing project of creating more study space at the Webster Library on the downtown campus.
Did you know that you can get any article in our print journal collection scanned and e-mailed to you as a PDF attachment? Read more about our .
If you have problems finding or accessing the journals in compact shelving, don’t hesitate to ask for help at one of our service desks.]]>

Exhibition in Webster Library: in the details
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i8_Nov_2012_16:58:00_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i8_Nov_2012_16:58:00_EST
EXHIBITION: in the details DATE: November 6, 2012 – December 4, 2012 WHERE: Webster Library Atrium Entrance
This exhibition features artifacts and photographic documentation from projects by Concordia undergraduate students in two Ceramics Special Topics Courses: Urban Clay (Winter 2012) and 2D3D Ceramic Monoprint (Fall 2012). The Urban Clay projects investigate new ways to encounter clay in the city through site-specific public art projects situated on Concordia’s downtown campus. The 2D3D projects combine print techniques with ceramic materials to explore ornament and color in the creation of rich complex surfaces.]]>

One for the Books (Webster Library Exhibition)
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i18_Jan_2013_11:26:23_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i18_Jan_2013_11:26:23_EST
Artists: Mitch Dixon, Sarah Galarneau, Jacquelin Heichert, Lamontagne, Amanda Laprade, Évlyne Laurin, Sally Lee
December 7, 2012 - January 4, 2013
One for the Books presents the recent work of seven artists exploring the artists’ book in various forms.
These works invite a close examination into the intimate and reflexive space of the page, at the same time referencing other spaces: the private and domestic space, the ruminating mind, the past as it infiltrates the realm of the present, nature, the internet, the body and the space within and around it and even fictional, alternate worlds that uncannily resemble our own.
Jenny LinPRIN 381A instructor]]>

New: Unattended Workstation Procedure
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i18_Oct_2012_16:51:19_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i18_Oct_2012_16:51:19_EDT
The Libraries’ public computer workstations are heavily used, especially during peak periods of the semester. For different reasons, some users leave public workstations unattended for a long period. This situation frustrates other users who are in need of workstations and prevents them from accessing library services and resources.
This procedure applies to computer workstations only, not study tables as they are too difficult to monitor.
The time limit on unattended computer workstations is 30 minutes.
When a student reports an unattended computer workstation, a staff member takes note of the workstation number and time.
30 minutes later, if the workstation is still left unattended, two staff members go back to the workstation and put personal belongings in a clear plastic bag and bring it to the Circulation Desk.
The following note is left at the workstation:
This workstation was left unattended on [DATE], from X:XX a.m./p.m. to X:XX a.m./p.m. Belongings were removed and can be picked up at the Circulation Desk.
Bags and notes are available at both information desks.
In order to claim items, a user needs to be able to describe what was removed.
Signage has been installed at workstations and in labs to inform users of this procedure.
This new procedure is also posted on the website under "".
]]>

A variety of important e-resources have been added to the Libraries' collections
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i16_Oct_2012_11:13:30_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i16_Oct_2012_11:13:30_EDT
In case you missed it… Concordia University Libraries have added a variety of important electronic resources to our collection over the past few months. These include the major abstract and citation database , as well as a number of archival collections that significantly expand the range of digitized primary source materials available to Concordia’s students and researchers: , , , , , , and . Keep checking the What’s New section of the library website to stay up-to-date with recent acquisitions!
More about each resource:
– A major abstract and citation database covering scientific, technical, medical and social sciences fields as well as the arts and humanities.
– Digitized collection of every significant English-language and foreign-language title printed in Great Britain during the eighteenth century, as well as important works from the Americas.
- Digitized collections of primary sources from the 'long' nineteenth century.
- High-resolution colour reproductions of the entire run of Vogue magazine from 1892 to the present.
- Full-image archive of magazines from the film, media and entertainment industries.
- Facsimile edition of the Financial Times from its first issue in 1888 up to four years ago.
- Digital archive of every page published by The Times of London from 1986-2006.
- Full-page reproductions of Toronto Star issues from 1894 up to three years ago.

We're pleased to announce that Microsoft Visio 2010 is now available on all standard public workstations (excluding laptops). Visio is a 2-D drawing application that’s part of the Microsoft Office Suite. It’s useful for creating diagrams, concept maps, project management diagrams and timelines (GANTT and PERT), business diagrams (Six Sigma, TQM, org charts), maps and floor plans, and flowcharts. It also creates and opens VDX files.]]>

New Business Research Guide
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i25_Sep_2012_16:01:46_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i25_Sep_2012_16:01:46_EDT
At the library, we’ve create a new “one stop shop” for Concordia business students at . It includes:
A search box that simultaneously searches the main business article databases (, , , and )
A list of the top databases we recommend for business students, providing quick access to reports, financials, ratios, news, and ratings
A list of the top answers for business students to help them find information on how to do research, how to cite properly using APA, NAICS codes, videos and more
Links to all business databases, arranged by subject and type
Links to more detailed research guides by discipline
You can also access this research guide by going to the “Research Guides by Subject” tab on the library website and then selecting “Business”. Please have a look and let us know if you have

INTERACTIONS at the Webster Library
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i4_Sep_2012_14:42:39_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i4_Sep_2012_14:42:39_EDT
It is with great pleasure that the Webster Library joins the Leonard & Bina Ellen Art Gallery in presenting Box, a video installation by Olivia Boudreau realized in 2009, with responses by Amelia Jones, Nicole Lattuca, and Claude Poissant.
This in situ installation is part of the exhibition INTERACTIONS, presented at the Leonard & Bina Ellen Art Gallery from August 30 to October 27, 2012. It provokes encounters between ten contemporary artworks and 30 participants to reveal various relations to art, in order to reflect on the reception and interpretation of contemporary art.
The Ellen Gallery is situated on the ground floor of the Library Building. It is open from Tuesday to Friday, 12 to 6 pm and Saturday, 12 to 5 pm.

Webster Library's current print journals in a new location
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i4_Jul_2012_16:00:41_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i4_Jul_2012_16:00:41_EDT
Webster Library’s current print journal subscriptions can be found on the 3rd floor of Webster Library near the Media Desk on two sets of shelves labelled in orange either Webster Journals or Webster Newspapers.
Most ongoing print subscriptions, including all scholarly journals, can be found in the Webster Journals location. You will find on these shelves the last 5 years’ worth of issues/volumes for each ongoing journal subscription or, in the case of all visual arts journals, the last 10 years’ worth of issues/volumes.
On the shelves labelled Webster Newspapers you will find the daily newspapers and a small collection of newsprint and trade publications which are eventually weeded (in some cases replaced by microform holdings).
You may find the
records for these publications unclear at present. This should be resolved by the fall. Should you need any assistance locating a journal title please ask for help at the .]]>

Exhibition in Webster Library: ex voto suscepto
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i4_Sep_2012_13:13:28_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i4_Sep_2012_13:13:28_EDT
EXHIBITION: ex voto suscepto ARTISTS: MFA Fibres students: Dana Dal Bo, Emily Jan, Kristin Nelson, Geneviève Moisan, jenna dawn maclellan, Caitlin Thompson, Sandra Smirle DATE: September 5, 2012 – October 4, 2012 WHERE: Webster Library Atrium
Much of the work in this exhibition was made in response to the time students spent in Oaxaca Mexico as part of an exchange through the Oax-i-fornmia programme. Some works are reflections on craft and on making; some respond directly to place and history, and others are literally or figuratively offerings to a modern-day divine; but all express gratitude for the opportunity to travel, to converse, to observe, to learn, to dwell for a short time with the landscape and the people of the Oaxaca valley.
Tin man.
Dana Dal Bo
Jumper.
Caitlin Thompson.
Melissa métier.
jenna dawn maclellan

Construction on De Maisonneuve throughout the summer
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i4_Jul_2012_12:47:37_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i4_Jul_2012_12:47:37_EDT
The City of Montreal is carrying out roadwork on De Maisonneuve Boulevard between Bishop and Mackay throughout the summer. This work is scheduled for completion on August 31.
As a result, visitors to the Webster Library may experience some noise, especially at the north end of the building. Those persons seeking quiet study areas are encourage to use the blue zones toward the south end of the library (away from De Maisonneuve).
Note also that, due to the construction, the Shuttle Bus stop is relocated to the northwest corner of Mackay and Ste-Catherine.

30 May 2012 17:44:23 EDT
Webster Library undergoing renovations
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i30_May_2012_17:44:23_EDT
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i30_May_2012_17:44:23_EDT
Renovations are now underway in the vicinity of the circulation desk on the
200 level of the Webster Library due to flooding caused by severe thunderstorms
at the end of May. This may generate some noise from time to time. Those
individuals seeking quiet study space are advised to make use of the blue study
zones on the 300 or 400 level. Thanks to all our library users for their
patience while these urgent renovations are being made.
Although the Library suffered water damage during the storm, it has been
confirmed that the damage was confined to the library's Circulation Services
area. It appears that no collection materials, books or personal belongings
were affected.
The library has set up a temporary circulation desk located on the second
floor of the Webster Library, and services will be restored during the day.
Overdue loan charges will not be assessed for the period during which the
library was closed.
Previously posted hours are in effect at the Webster and Vanier Libraries.
Summer term hours: June 4 to August 10, 2012
Thanks go to all those people who have assisted university staff in dealing
with this situation - and to those who offered!  ]]>

2012-03-12
Call for Proposals: Concordia University Libraries Annual Research Forum
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i20_Feb_2012_13:57:27_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i20_Feb_2012_13:57:27_EST
Concordia University Libraries will hold its 10th annual Library Research Forum on April 27, 2012 from 9:00 am to 12:30 at the Loyola Jesuit Hall and Conference Centre, 7141 Sherbrooke Street West. Gwendolyn Ebbett, University Librarian at the University of Windsor, will deliver a keynote presentation. Proposals are welcome for presentations or posters on research in any area of library and information studies. More information and the presentation/poster proposal form can be found here: . Lunch will be served after the Forum.
Since 2002, the Research Forum (formerly the Library Poster Forum) has provided librarians, archivists, and information professionals with an opportunity to describe and promote their completed or in-progress research, to seek suggestions for enhancing their research interests, to identify potential new partners for projects, to test the effectiveness of their undertakings, and to promote research activities within the academic library community.
The Forum is also designed to showcase a diversity of research interests with a goal of highlighting the process of research. Accordingly, presentations or posters may reflect any stage or aspect of a librarian’s research including conceptualization, planning, data gathering, compilation, and findings. Faculty and graduate students from both of Montreal’s library schools are also invited. Presentations may be made in either English or French.
Concordia University Libraries Annual Research Forum
Date: Friday, April 27, 2012 Time: 9:00 am - 12:30 pm Location: Loyola Jesuit Hall and Conference Centre, 7141 Sherbrooke Street West See also:
from previous Forums]]>

My Reading Lists and My History now available in CLUES
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i21_Feb_2012_12:39:57_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i21_Feb_2012_12:39:57_EST
As of Tuesday, February 21, two new features are available in CLUES, the library catalogue:
An optional “My Reading History” feature will remember the titles that you have borrowed from the library.  To enable this feature, you must specifically opt in after you login to your MyCLUES account. Please read the Privacy Disclaimer in MyCLUES before you opt in.
A “My Lists” feature will allow you to create, save, and manage lists of titles in your MyCLUES account.
For more information, please visit .  We hope you will enjoy trying out these new features!]]>

Webster Library Entrance Focus Group Invitation
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i6_Feb_2012_15:26:03_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i6_Feb_2012_15:26:03_EST
Dear Students,
The Webster Library entrance will be redesigned to better suit your needs. In order to create an optimal space, we would love for you to share your ideas about the library entrance area (along the atrium on LB2)! A series of plans have been drawn up as options for our new entrance. If you are interested in participating in the library redesign, we would love to hear your thoughts on our new plans and the future “look” of your library. One-hour focus group meetings will be taking place in March at Webster Library room LB-340 to assess the new plans. If you are available we would love for you to join us. The dates are as follows:
For undergraduate students
Monday, March 5, 10 am to 11 am
Monday, March 5, 1 pm to 2 pm
Thursday, March 8, 10 am to 11 am
For graduate students
Thursday, March 8, 1 pm to 2 pm
We would like to thank you in advance for your involvement in our library project. We look forward to hearing what you have to say!  For more information on the project and/or to RSVP for one of the above time slots please contact Karen at .
Sincerely,
Guylaine Beaudry Director, Webster Library

Exhibition: Petite Enveloppe Urbaine (19) : AMANEUNSIS
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#guid=http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i14_Feb_2012_10:46:05_EST
http://library.concordia.ca/about/news/#i14_Feb_2012_10:46:05_EST
EXHIBITION: Petite Enveloppe Urbaine (19): AMANEUNSIS ARTIST: Felicity Tayler DATE: February
10, 2012 – March 16, 2012 WHERE: Webster Library Atrium
Petite enveloppe urbaine No. 19 contains the answers to the questions posed by fifty-seven people in different cities. Responses were found in the esoteric collection of the Prelinger Library (San Francisco) and arranged in this issue of Petite Enveloppe Urbaine as a narrative landscape, interpolating the history of communities and their relationship to the environment.
Double page spread from Petite enveloppe urbaine no. 19, Amanuensis, 2011.]]>

is a full-image online archive of every page published by The Times of London from 1986-2006, complementing the Times Digital Archive 1785-1985 already available at Concordia. The text within the page images is fully searchable at the article level. Users can easily search news articles, obituaries, advertising and classifieds. is a fully-searchable facsimile edition of the Financial Times offering the complete run of the London edition of the paper, from its first issue in 1888 up to four years ago.
